<script>
  function DOMTokenListSupports(tokenList, token) {
    if (!tokenList || !tokenList.supports) {
      return false;
    }
    try {
      return tokenList.supports(token);
    } catch (e) {
      if (e instanceof TypeError) {
        console.log('The DOMTokenList doesn\'t have a supported tokens list.', e);
      } else {
        console.error('That shouldn\'t have happened.', e);
      }
    }
  };

  function loadAdLib(script) {
    if (!window.__AdLib) {
      
        var domainEnv = '.vice.com';
      
      var adLibScript = document.createElement('script');
      adLibScript.src = script;
      adLibScript.id = 'ad-lib';
      adLibScript.onload = () => {
        if (window.__AdLib) {
          window.__AdLib.env = 'production';
          window.__AdLib.template = 'article';
          window.__AdLib.site = 'vice';
          window.__AdLib.brand = 'vice';
          window.__AdLib.domain = domainEnv;
          window.__AdLib.init();
        }
      }
      adLibScript.onerror = (e) => {
        console.error('Ad-Lib could not load it\'s script.', e);
      }
      document.head.appendChild(adLibScript);
    }
  }

  var linkSupportsPreload = DOMTokenListSupports(document.createElement('link').relList, 'preload');

  if (!linkSupportsPreload) {
    console.log('linkSupportsPreload not supported!');
    loadAdLib('https://vice-web-statics-cdn.vice.com/vendor/ad-lib/v2.3.1/vice-ad-lib.js');
  }
</script>

  window.__APOLLO_STATE = {"Article:5c1041ff402a660006c8bb17":{"id":"5c1041ff402a660006c8bb17","body":"\u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003ESLAUGHTERHOUSE BIG FIVE:\u003Cbr\u003EEVERYTHING WAS UGLY AND NOTHING WORKED\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIt was just before closing time at a Verizon store in Bushwick, New York last May when I burst through the door, sweaty and exasperated. I had just sprintedokay I walked, but \u003Ci\u003E briskly\u003C\u002Fi\u003Efrom another Verizon outlet a few blocks away in the hopes Id make it before they closed shop for the night. I was looking for a SIM card that would fit a refurbished 2012 Samsung Galaxy S3 that I had recently purchased on eBay, but the previous three Verizon stores I visited didnt have any chips that would fit such an old model.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen I explained my predicament to the salesperson, he laughed in my face. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EYou want to switch from you current phone to an... \u003Ci\u003E S3\u003C\u002Fi\u003E? he asked incredulously.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI explained my situation. I was about to embark on a month without intentionally using any services or products produced by the so-called Big Five tech companies: Amazon, Apple, Facebook, Google, and Microsoft. At that point I had found adequate, open source replacements for most of the services offered by these companies, but ditching the Android OS, which is developed by Google, was proving difficult.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMost of the tech I use on a day-to-day basis is pretty utilitarian. At the time I was using a cheap ASUS laptop at work and a homebrew PC at my apartment. My phone was a Verizon-specific version of the Samsung Galaxy J3, a 2016 model that cost a little over $100 new. They weren't fancy, but theyve reliably met most of my needs for years. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EFor the past week and a half I had spent most of my evenings trying to port an independent mobile OS called Sailfish onto my phone without any luck. As it turned out, Verizon had locked the bootloader on my phone model, which is so obscure that no one in the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fforum.xda-developers.com\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Evibrant Android hacking community\u003C\u002Fa\u003E had dedicated much time to figuring out a workaround. If I wanted to use Sailfish, I was going to have to get a different phone.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI remembered using a Galaxy S3 while living in India a few years ago and liking it well enough. I ultimately decided to go with that model after finding extensive documentation online from others who had had success porting unofficial operating systems onto their phones. So two days and $20-plus-shipping later, I was in possession of a surprisingly new-looking Verizon Galaxy S3. The only thing that remained to do before loading Sailfish onto the device was to find a SIM card that fit. SIM cards come in three different sizesstandard, micro, and nanoand my nano SIM wouldnt fit in the S3s micro SIM port. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EBy the time I explained all this to the Verizon employee, he had found a SIM card that would work. As he navigated the Android setup menu he asked me if I wanted him to link my Google account to the phone. Oh thats right, he said, looking up from the phone and laughing. Sorry, its just a habit.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI could hardly blame him for the slipup. Im probably the only person who has ever come into the store who didnt want to synchronize the Google services they use with their phone. Itd be senseless to resist that kind of convenience and Google knows this, which is why Android prompts you to enter your Google credentials before youve even reached the phones dashboard for the first time. But what I wanted to know is whether there was another way.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E Want a more in-depth explanation of why you might want to quit the Big Five? Check out my \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fmbxndq\u002Fone-month-without-big-five-microsoft-google-facebook-apple-amazon\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Cb\u003E introductory blog post\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003Cb\u003E on how this experiment came about \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EBy now, its common knowledge that Google, Facebook, and Amazon are harvesting as much of our personal data as they can get their hands on to feed us targeted ads, train artificial intelligence, and\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.forbes.com\u002Fsites\u002Fkashmirhill\u002F2012\u002F02\u002F16\u002Fhow-target-figured-out-a-teen-girl-was-pregnant-before-her-father-did\u002F#26cf0de86668\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E sell us things before we know we need them\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The results of this ruthless data-driven hypercapitalism speak for themselves: Today, the Big Five tech companies are worth a combined total of $3 trillion dollars. When I started my month without the Big Five in May, Googles parent company Alphabet, Amazon, and Apple were \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftechcrunch.com\u002F2018\u002F07\u002F23\u002Fgoogle-joins-the-race-to-1-trillion\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eracing\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to be the first company in history with stock worth $1 trillion. In August, Apple became the first to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnbc.com\u002F2018\u002F08\u002F02\u002Fapple-hits-1-trillion-in-market-value.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ereach this milestone\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and just a few weeks later Amazons market cap \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnbc.com\u002F2018\u002F09\u002F04\u002Famazon-hits-1-trillion-in-market-value.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ealso briefly passed $1 trillion\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWith the exception of Microsoft and Apple, these fortunes were not built by selling wildly popular products, but by collecting massive amounts of user data in order to more effectively sell us stuff. At the same time, this data has also been abused to swing elections and abet state surveillance. For most of us, giving away our data was seen as the price of convenienceGoogle and Facebook are free to use, after all. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough Amazon now sells its own products, its rapid growth was fueled by selling other peoples products. This gave the company unprecedented access to consumer habits and data, which it used to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2018\u002F11\u002F15\u002Fstyle\u002Fthis-is-also-amazon.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Espin out its own consumer goods brands\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and gain invaluable experience in logistics and web hosting. Both its in-house consumer brands and Amazon Web Services are now core parts of Amazon.\u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThe widespread adoption of Microsoft and Apple products over the past 40 years, meanwhile, was no accident, but the result of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.theregister.co.uk\u002F2018\u002F11\u002F27\u002Fapple_supreme_court\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emonopoly-focused business tactics\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The end result was that their products appear to be a natural default. Youre either a Mac person or a Windows person and you stick to your brand because thats the way its always been.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv data-iframely-id=\"zkbhEKe\" data-embedded-url=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=cO0-VJbNOR8\" class=\"article__embed article__embed--iframely\"\u003E\u003Cdiv style=\"left:0;width:100%;height:0;position:relative;padding-bottom:75.0019%;\" data-iframely-smart-iframe=\"true\"\u003E\u003Ciframe data-img=\"\" data-iframely-url=\"\u002F\u002Foembed.vice.com\u002FzkbhEKe?playerjs=1&amp;media=1\" style=\"border:0;top:0;left:0;width:100%;height:100%;position:absolute;\" allowfullscreen=\"\" allow=\"autoplay; encrypted-media\" data-iframely-smart-iframe=\"true\" frameborder=\"0\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fiframe\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAs the open internet was swallowed whole by the megacorporations of Silicon Valley, however, a revolution was occurring in free, open source software (FOSS). Although FOSS can trace its roots back to the crew working at MITs artificial intelligence laboratory in the early 1980s, it broke into the mainstream in a big way largely due to the creation of Linux, an open operating system developed in the early 90s. These days theres a galaxy of free and open source software that offers adequate alternatives to most Big Five services, and much of it is powered by Linux. In fact, a lot of the Big Five services you use on a daily basis are probably also based on Linux or open source software that has had some proprietary code grafted on top of it before it was repackaged and sold back to you.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMy goal with going a month without the Big Five was to see if I could rely solely on open source or independent software without compromising what I was able to accomplish with proprietary code. Basically, could I live my normal life with open source alternatives? \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EGoing into the experiment, I realized that there was a good chance Id come crawling back to some of the Big Five services when it was over. Yet as I discovered over the four weeks, switching to independent alternatives didnt negatively affect most parts of my life, but it did take a little getting used to.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EBefore diving into the nitty gritty of what worked and what didnt, however, let me explain the limits of the experiment.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E LIMITATIONS\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAfter \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fmbxndq\u002Fone-month-without-big-five-microsoft-google-facebook-apple-amazon\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eannouncing my intention\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to relinquish Big Five services for a month, People On The Internet pointed out that my experiment would fail because I would almost certainly visit a website hosted by Amazons cloud service at some point, thereby indirectly putting money into Jeff Bezoss pocket. This is, of course, true. Amazon Web Services hosts a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.zdnet.com\u002Farticle\u002F15-sites-you-know-that-you-may-not-know-are-based-on-amazon-web-services\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Enumber of popular sites\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that I use on a regular basis, such as Netflix, Reddit, Spotify, SoundCloud, and Yelp, all of which I visited at least once during the month. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EUnfortunately, avoiding this kind of indirect support of Big Five through their back-end services will become even more difficult to avoid in the future. For example, Google is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.datacenterknowledge.com\u002Fgoogle-alphabet\u002Fthree-new-submarine-cables-link-google-cloud-data-centers\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ebeginning to lay its own undersea internet cables\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, creating the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.reuters.com\u002Farticle\u002Fus-google-nest\u002Fgoogles-nest-launches-network-technology-for-connected-home-idUSKBN0FK0JX20140715\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Einfrastructure for totally networked homes\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fxygk4w\u002Fgoogle-self-driving-cars-waymo\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Edeveloping self-driving car services\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Microsoft is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fpavq99\u002Fmicrosoft-project-natick-submarine-data-center\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eaggressively pursuing cloud computing platforms\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fywen8x\u002F13000-projects-ditched-github-for-gitlab-monday-morning\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Erecently acquired GitHub\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a code repository I frequently use while teaching myself how to program. \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Faws.amazon.com\u002Fblogs\u002Faws\u002Faws-ground-station-ingest-and-process-data-from-orbiting-satellites\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EAmazon moved into the space data business\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and is also working on \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fevng4p\u002Fhack-that-turns-amazon-echo-into-a-spying-device-cant-be-fixed-by-software-patch\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Enetworking your home with devices like Alexa\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and Facebook \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fzm539j\u002Fwhatsapp-founder-brian-acton-sellout-instagram-facebook\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Estill controls how much of the world communicates\u003C\u002Fa\u003E through its website, Instagram, and WhatsApp. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EYet even if I did scrupulously avoid visiting sites hosted on Amazon Web Services, the experiment was designed to be temporary. This meant that rather than shutting down my work Gmail accounts, I had them forward my email to an alternative email provider that I would then use to send and receive emails. There were also inevitably important files that I neglected to transfer from my Google Drive to an alternative hosting service when I was preparing for the experiment, so I had to log in to my Google account to retrieve those files and move them over. Or there were times when I was attempting to change a YouTube link to a HookTube link and accidentally landed on YouTube.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI dont think the handful of lapses alluded to above undercut the spirit of the experiment, however, since I wasnt intentionally using any services offered by the Big Five. If I were permanently planning to leave the Big Five I would have transferred \u003Ci\u003E all \u003C\u002Fi\u003Emy files from Google Drive, deleted my Gmail accounts, and so on. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ESo with these experimental limitations in mind, I present the Motherboard Guide to Quitting the Big Five, based on my own experience in May 2018. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E THE MOTHERBOARD GUIDE \u003Cbr\u003ETO QUITTING THE BIG FIVE\u003Cbr\u003E \u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__media\"\u003E \u003Cpicture class=\"article__image\"\u003E \u003Csource media=\"(max-width: 25em)\" srcset=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD\u002FACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=\" srcset=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD\u002FACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=\" src=\"data:image\u002Fgif;base64,R0lGODlhAQABAAD\u002FACwAAAAAAQABAAACADs=\" alt=\"1544569811922-1524514817075-drake_tech\" class=\"col-12-xs\" data-src=\"https:\u002F\u002Fvideo-images.vice.com\u002F_uncategorized\u002F1544569811922-1524514817075-drake_tech.jpeg\"\u003E \u003C\u002Fpicture\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"article__image-caption\"\u003EImage: Motherboard\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003EHOW TO QUIT FACEBOOK\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMy experiment in leaving the Big Five arguably began back in March, when I\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fa3yz9k\u002Fhow-to-delete-your-facebook-permanently\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E deleted my Facebook account in the wake of the Cambridge Analytica scandal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Of all the companies I abandoned for this experiment, Facebook and its subsidiaries were by far the easiest. I have tried and failed to start an Instagram account several times over the years. I find Instagram unbelievably boring and Ive come to terms with the fact that Ill never understand its already large, and still growing, appeal. \u003Cbr\u003E\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EQuitting WhatsApp was more difficult since I used it to keep in touch with my friends abroad, many of whom live in countries where WhatsApp is the default communication tool. With friends and family in the US, I switched over to the encrypted chat app Telegram or just stuck to normal SMS and email. As I soon learned, the ideal messaging platform doesnt exist. If security is your thing, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fqvmgzp\u002Ffacebook-sheryl-sandberg-committed-whatsapp-encryption\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EWhatsApp\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fvv73w8\u002Fwhy-its-harder-to-encrypt-facebook-messenger-than-whatsapp\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EMessenger\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fbj3pxd\u002Fsignal-disappearing-messages-not-disappearing\" target=\"_blank\"\u003ESignal\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002F53da7k\u002Fthis-is-how-russian-spies-could-crack-telegram\" target=\"_blank\"\u003ETelegram\u003C\u002Fa\u003E all have their flaws and all offer comparable services. The main advantage of WhatsApp is that \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftechcrunch.com\u002F2018\u002F01\u002F31\u002Fwhatsapp-hits-1-5-billion-monthly-users-19b-not-so-bad\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Enearly a quarter of the world already uses it\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI have been off Facebook for a few months now and my only regret is that I didnt leave sooner. Although there is admittedly something of a phantom-limb effect right after leavingpulling out my phone in response to imaginary pings from Messenger or reflexively navigating to the Facebook login page only to realize I no longer had a profilethe feeling that I was always missing something quickly subsided. I go out with friends and attend events just as much as I did before. I have no qualms about missing events that I wouldve received a mass Facebook invite to because now I live in blissful ignorance of their occurrence. Contrary to my expectations, my FOMO is at its lowest point in years.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp class=\"article__pull-quote\"\u003EContrary to my expectations, my FOMO is at its lowest point in years\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAdmittedly, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftheoutline.com\u002Fpost\u002F4040\u002Fyou-cant-just-tell-everyone-to-leave-facebook?zd=1&amp;zi=hy6stgm3\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eleaving Facebook is a privilege\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. In many places, Facebook and Messenger are peoples only links to the outside world, or people may depend on Facebook to run their business. It can also make it challenging for people to contact you if you leave. Although I made a point of collecting contact information from my friends before I deleted my account, there were inevitably some I forgot. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDuring my month without the Big Five, I received an email from an Argentinian friend I hadnt seen in years who was passing through New York. When we met for dinner, he mentioned how hard I had been to track down without Facebook. Fortunately, Ive listed my email publicly on my website and still had a Twitter profile at that point, so he was able to find an alternative method of contacting me. But for people who dont work in industries where its normal to make your email public or to have a personal website, these types of missed connections are bound to happen.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAs for the actual process of deleting your Facebook profile, its pretty simple. Ive \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fa3yz9k\u002Fhow-to-delete-your-facebook-permanently\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ecovered the process in detail in another article\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, but there are a few points youll want to consider before taking the plunge. If youre the type of person who signs up for other apps such as Tinder or Airbnb with your Facebook account, then deleting your Facebook profile is going to be way more of a pain in the ass because youre going to have to switch all those accounts over to an email login first. Second, if you have hundreds of photo albums dating back to 2008 that you want to save, be prepared to spend a few hours scraping them off of Facebook. (There are scripts that help with this, but I didnt find any of them to be that efficient.) Other than that, theres a button on Facebook that will allow you to download all your data in one fell swoop. It includes every like, comment, and event invite from the past decade so you can cherish these internet minutiae until you grow old and die.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E Read More: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fj5zap3\u002Fdelete-all-your-apps\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Cb\u003E Delete All Your Apps\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThere are a number of legitimate reasons you might want to consider leaving Facebook. In my case, I left due to my discomfort with the idea that I was giving away huge amounts of intensely personal data to a company that had a history of mishandling its users information. I was also getting tired of wasting so much time endlessly scrolling through status updates from people whom I hadnt seen or talked to for years. I had managed to convince myself that clicking like on digital simulacra of peoples lives was socializing and, to borrow Mark Zuckerbergs favorite word, being part of a community. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ETheres no doubt that humans are social creatures and that human interaction is a critical part of an individuals wellbeing. How strange, then, that a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnbc.com\u002F2018\u002F11\u002F12\u002Fcutting-back-on-social-media-reduces-loneliness-depression-study-finds.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emounting body of evidence shows that reducing social media use actually \u003Ci\u003Edecreases \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eloneliness and feelings of unhappiness\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. To make matters worse, sometimes \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2014\u002F06\u002F30\u002Ftechnology\u002Ffacebook-tinkers-with-users-emotions-in-news-feed-experiment-stirring-outcry.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EFacebook makes us unhappy on purpose\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EBut even if you have more free time than you know what to do with and dont mind forking over your data to a multi-billion dollar company that just \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.youtube.com\u002Fwatch?v=GGTWUOxkfGQ\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eruns ads\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, you might consider ditching Facebook because \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.washingtonpost.com\u002Ftechnology\u002F2018\u002F07\u002F31\u002Ffacebook-says-it-has-uncovered-coordinated-disinformation-operation-ahead-midterm-elections\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eit is a breeding ground for disinformation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. In the past three years, evidence has emerged that Facebook was a primary vector for sowing political discord in the United States and, so far, Zuckerberg hasnt demonstrated that his company has the faintest idea of how to stop it. Maybe one day it will figure out an effective filter for fake news, but until then, theres a good chance that meme your racist uncle just posted was generated by a Russian bot.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E Read More: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fxwk9zd\u002Fhow-facebook-content-moderation-works\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Cb\u003E The Impossible Job: Inside Facebooks Struggle to Moderate 2 Billion People\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDuring \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.theguardian.com\u002Ftechnology\u002F2018\u002Fapr\u002F11\u002Fmark-zuckerbergs-testimony-to-congress-the-key-moments\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EZuckerbergs testimony before the US Congress\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in April, Senator Lindsey Graham asked him point blank whether Facebook was a monopoly. Zuckerberg danced around the question and was ultimately unable to provide an example of alternative services offering a similar product to Facebook. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough there are lots of alternative social media platforms out there, none of them are used by half the worlds population, which is exactly what makes Facebook so valuable. Still, if you want to keep social media in your life, you might want to use an alternative platform, such as \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002F783akg\u002Fmastodon-is-like-twitter-without-nazis-so-why-are-we-not-using-it\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EMastodon\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (a decentralized Twitter imitator) or \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002F3dkbb3\u002Fyou-are-not-a-product-ello-wants-to-be-the-anti-facebook-social-network\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EEllo\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (a privacy-oriented, ad-free Facebook alternative). You wont find anyone you know on there, probably, but at least your social media fix wont come at the cost of your privacy.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E HOW TO QUIT APPLE\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIve only owned two Apple products in my life. One was an old 120 gigabyte iPod classic that I still miss dearly. The other was an iPhone 4 that I got in 2010 and had for a year and a half before I switched to Android and never looked back. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ESince I didnt have any Apple products to relinquish for my monthlong experiment, I used the time for a little introspection on why I dislike Apple products. The main reason is that I was raised using Windows, so I was disincentivized to learn the quirks of a new OS. As I grew older, however, I also found Apples walled-garden approach to its device ecosystem infuriating. (For many people, however, this closed ecosystem and interoperability between Apple devices is exactly what makes its products attractive.) \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EApples obsession with total control is perhaps best exemplified by the release of iPhone 7 in 2016, which got rid of the ubiquitous headphone jack that has been used by literally every other digital device since forever and replaced it with a proprietary dongle. This was an affront to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnet.com\u002Fnews\u002Fapple-is-obviously-a-cult-and-samsung-isnt-says-cultural-historian\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EApples devout followers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, sure, but that didnt stop the company from selling more than\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.statista.com\u002Fstatistics\u002F263401\u002Fglobal-apple-iphone-sales-since-3rd-quarter-2007\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E 200 million iPhones last year\u003C\u002Fa\u003E at around $600 a pop. And yet here we are, years after Apple adopted the dongle, and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.fastcompany.com\u002F90270691\u002Fi-still-miss-my-headphone-jack-and-i-want-it-back\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Epeople are still mourning the loss of the headphone jack\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI know why \u003Ci\u003E I \u003C\u002Fi\u003Edont use Apple, but even after a month of thinking about it, I still couldnt rationalize why anyone would spend a night sleeping outside an Apple store to get their hands on one of its overpriced products. People love to justify their purchase of iPhones by appealing to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.tomsguide.com\u002Fus\u002Fandroid-google-ios-security-report,news-26783.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ethe superior security of iOS compared to Android\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. But recent updates have \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnet.com\u002Fnews\u002Fgoogle-android-is-just-as-secure-as-ios-iphone-david-kleidermacher\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Esignificantly closed the security gap\u003C\u002Fa\u003E between Android phones and iPhones.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E\u003Cp class=\"article__pull-quote\"\u003EAfter a month of thinking about it, I still couldnt rationalize why anyone would spend a night sleeping outside an Apple store to get their hands on one of its overpriced products\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EUnfortunately, there are no independent studies about what motivates most people to buy Apple phones, but I suspect that security probably wouldnt top the list. Besides, as the\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002F8q8qbv\u002Fneither-apple-nor-doj-will-back-down-in-new-york-iphone-case\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E fallout between the FBI and Apple over backdoors\u003C\u002Fa\u003E reminded us, theres no such thing as an unhackable device. In fact, theres a\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fvbxxxd\u002Funlock-iphone-ios11-graykey-grayshift-police\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E relatively cheap hacking tool that can be used by cops to bypass iPhone encryption\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Even when Apple tried to fix this with a patch, iPhones \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fpavwzv\u002Fcops-are-confident-iphone-hackers-have-found-a-workaround-to-apples-new-security-feature\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Egot hacked again anyway\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003Ci\u003E Cest la vie\u003C\u002Fi\u003E!\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOkay, but what about Macs? Apples laptops and desktop computers are usually adored for their performance specs and native applications that are geared toward creative types (GarageBand, iMovie, etc.). Apple knows this, which is why a recent \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftvadvertsongs.com\u002Fapple-behind-the-mac\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ecommercial\u003C\u002Fa\u003E campaign for MacBook features artists making art while a Daniel Johnston song called Story of an Artist plays in the background. Very subtle. The thing is, you can build a custom PC that matches or surpasses the technical specs of a high-end Mac without spending $5,000.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDespite what \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fkb7g8w\u002Fpc-gaming-is-still-way-too-hard\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eyou may have heard\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, building a custom PC is not as hard as it sounds. Its basically just an expensive and delicate form of electronic Lego. I dont have any formal experience in computer science and I was able to build a decent PC with 2 GPUs, 16 gigs of memory, two terabytes of storage, and a quad-core CPU for around $1,000 by using handy tools such as \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpcpartpicker.com\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EPC Part Picker\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. My PC has way more power than Ive ever needed and still costs less than a new MacBook and far less than a Mac desktop. As for the Macs native applications, most of these have fine Linux equivalents. For example, heres an extensive list of \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Flinux-sound.org\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Efree sound and MIDI software\u003C\u002Fa\u003E for Linux; \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fubuntustudio.org\u002Ftour\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EUbuntu Studio\u003C\u002Fa\u003E is great for most video editing needs; there are even \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Falternativeto.net\u002Fsoftware\u002Fsiri\u002F?license=free\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eseveral open source alternatives to Siri\u003C\u002Fa\u003E.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E HOW TO QUIT AMAZON\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDepending on how you look at it, Amazon is either the hardest or the easiest company to quit of the Big Five. On the one hand, its consumer-facing business is mostly predicated on the idea of convenience, as evidenced by products like the Dash button or Alexa. This should, in principle, make it easy to quit since it would only require going back to the old ways of buying things from an actual brick-and-mortar store or visiting websites that sell specific goods. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhen I started my experiment, I had an Amazon Prime account, but really only used Amazon to regularly buy three things: Books, cat food, and cat litter. As someone who exclusively uses public transportation, these items are a pain to buy at a store and transfer to my house because they are large and heavy. Of course I could just order the cat products from another site, but Amazon Prime offers free shipping and the ability to set up recurring automatic orders.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E Read More: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fgy7j4q\u002Fhow-to-get-amazon-prime-for-free-cancel-prime\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Cb\u003E How To Get Amazon Prime for Free for Life\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDuring my experiment, however, I was determined to patronize my locally owned pet store since this seemed to be the most antithetical to Amazons dominance of all things retail. Carrying these items the few blocks to my house sucked (a box of cat litter weighs 40 pounds), but what blew even more was the price difference. The same cat food I always buy on Amazon cost more than twice as much at my local pet store. While this was fine for a month, I couldnt afford this large of an increase in my expenses in the long term. My best bet, then, would be to still buy the pet items I needed online from websites such as Chewy, which still provide most of the convenience offered by Amazon.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIt wasnt convenience alone that made Amazon into the behemoth it is todaythere were plenty of online book retailers around when Amazon hit the scene in 1994. What made Amazon successful was that its catalog included books not carried by other (online) bookstores. Over the past two decades, it has expanded this logic to every type of consumer good and this is precisely what makes \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2013\u002F10\u002F29\u002Fbooks\u002Fthe-everything-store-jeff-bezos-and-the-age-of-amazon.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ethe everything store\u003C\u002Fa\u003E so difficult to quit. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWhereas a brick-and-mortar store can only carry a finite inventory, Amazons inventory is effectively limitless. This combination of infinite selection and total convenience is exactly the type of selling point that appeals to Americas workforce, which is increasingly strapped for both time and money. For people living in rural areas or with disabilities, Amazons rapid delivery services can \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2018\u002F12\u002F08\u002Fopinion\u002Fsunday\u002Fhate-amazon-try-living-without-it.html?fbclid=IwAR3JeHGLloNWPPTAgWxOmPr71ZY9Fi3ptMBhXSBO1xovnb7-MAAUqGKIg6g\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ealso be a lifeline\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI am able-bodied and live in one of the largest cities in the world, so quitting Amazon is arguably a privilege. I didnt mind calling my local bookstore to ask it to order a particular title or popping into the local pet store every few weeks if thats what it took to cut the company from my life. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThen one day I was making a recipe that called for pine nuts, only to discover that none of the three grocery stores in my neighborhood carried them. The only other grocery store remotely close to me was Whole Foods, which was recently acquired by Amazon and definitely carried pine nuts. So I caved, dear reader, and bought some overpriced seeds from an Amazon subsidiary.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough shopping local or going to other online stores is an option for quitting Amazon, some of its other subsidiaries are far more difficult to replace because they are unique. I dont game, but if I did it \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2018\u002F06\u002F17\u002Fbusiness\u002Fmedia\u002Famazon-twitch-video-games.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ewould be hard to find an adequate replacement for Twitch\u003C\u002Fa\u003E because so many gamers already use it. Likewise, the Internet Movie Database for movie facts and Goodreads for book reviews are two online destinations for which there isnt an adequate alternative and are basically \u003Ci\u003E the\u003C\u002Fi\u003E go-to sites for their respective domains. Finally, as mentioned earlier, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.zdnet.com\u002Farticle\u002F15-sites-you-know-that-you-may-not-know-are-based-on-amazon-web-services\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emany major websites\u003C\u002Fa\u003E such as Netflix and Spotify run on Amazon Web Services, so if you use these services youre also indirectly supporting Amazon.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003ENevertheless, there are plenty of good reasons to limit your patronage of Amazon and its subsidiaries. For starters, Amazon has become notorious for its mistreatment of workers. A 2015 \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2015\u002F08\u002F16\u002Ftechnology\u002Finside-amazon-wrestling-big-ideas-in-a-bruising-workplace.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Ci\u003E New York Times\u003C\u002Fi\u003E expose\u003C\u002Fa\u003E detailed the grueling expectations placed on Amazons white collar workers, and \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.latimes.com\u002Fopinion\u002Ftopoftheticket\u002Fla-na-tt-amazon-brutal-workplace-20150818-story.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Estory\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after \u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fwww.businessinsider.com\u002Famazon-warehouse-workers-share-their-horror-stories-2018-4\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Estory\u003C\u002Fa\u003E after \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.salon.com\u002F2014\u002F02\u002F23\u002Fworse_than_wal_mart_amazons_sick_brutality_and_secret_history_of_ruthlessly_intimidating_workers\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Estory\u003C\u002Fa\u003E keeps bubbling up that details the inhumane conditions faced by Amazons warehouse employees. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EYou may also take issue with \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2018\u002F06\u002F22\u002Fbusiness\u002Fdealbook\u002Famazon-staff-facial-recognition-protest.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EAmazons development of facial recognition software\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that is used for predictive policing and the companys support of similar products made by companies such as Palantir that use its cloud hosting service. Even if Amazons Echo and Dot are ostensibly benign, they are also liable to be hacked and \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fevng4p\u002Fhack-that-turns-amazon-echo-into-a-spying-device-cant-be-fixed-by-software-patch\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eturned into spy devices\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EFinally, Amazon has \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.fastcompany.com\u002F3066110\u002Fis-amazon-killing-jobs-and-destroying-communities\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Edeveloped a reputation for steamrolling\u003C\u002Fa\u003E local economies and may end up \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.marketwatch.com\u002Fstory\u002Famazon-is-going-to-kill-more-american-jobs-than-china-did-2017-01-19\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ekilling over 2 million jobs\u003C\u002Fa\u003E as it increases its dominance over traditional retail and other market sectors.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E HOW TO QUIT MICROSOFT\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI have used Microsofts operating system for as long as I can remember. My familys first computer ran Windows 95, but the first experience I can recall with a computer was Windows 98 and the boot theme mustve imprinted itself on my impressionable, 5-year-old brain because Ive exclusively used Windows ever since. The Vista and XP years were rough, Ill admit, but its always darkest before dawn. Windows 10 certainly has its flaws (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.pcworld.com\u002Farticle\u002F2971725\u002Fwindows\u002Fhow-to-reclaim-your-privacy-in-windows-10-piece-by-piece.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eespecially when it comes to privacy\u003C\u002Fa\u003E), but Id be lying if I said I wasnt dreading swapping it out for Ubuntu, a popular Linux distribution.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDeveloped as an open source operating system by Linus Torvalds in the early 90s, Linux has grown from a nerdy curiosity to a defining feature of modern computer systems. Indeed, Google, Microsoft, Amazon, and Facebook \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.linuxfoundation.org\u002Fmembership\u002Fmembers\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eare all major donors to the Linux foundation\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which underscores their reliance on the kernel. These days \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.zdnet.com\u002Farticle\u002Flinux-foundation-finds-enterprise-linux-growing-at-windows-expense\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ethe Linux kernel powers around 75 percent of cloud platforms\u003C\u002Fa\u003E and is also found at the core of many consumer-facing devices, including every phone using Android, which is the most popular mobile OS in the world by a huge margin. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough Linux is prized by system admins everywhere for its versatility, its been slow to catch on as an operating system for average PC users who mostly use their computers for web browsing, word processing, and other simple tasks. In the beginning, Linux was still very experimental and didnt offer equivalents for many of the standard programs found on Windows PCs or Macs. Further, many popular programs didnt bother to create a version of their software that could be used on machines running Linux. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EToday, things are much better in this respect. There are Linux equivalents of everything from Microsoft Office to Adobes Photoshop, and popular applications such as Spotify usually offer a Linux version of their software.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EPrior to this experiment, my only experience with Linux was \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002F59zdjq\u002Fan-idiots-guide-to-building-an-ethereum-mining-rig\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Esetting up a cryptocurrency mining rig\u003C\u002Fa\u003E that ran a custom operating system called EthOS specifically designed for mining. This familiarized me with some basic terminal commands, but really I was a total Linux noob. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EFortunately, getting Linux up and running on my laptop and home PC was pretty easy. For the laptop, I used a colleagues 2010 Alienware gaming laptop. Rather than partitioning the hard drive, which is a way to have multiple operating systems on a single computer, I opted to erase Windows and have the laptop only run Ubuntu.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003ETo do this, I \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.ubuntu.com\u002Fdownload\u002Fdesktop\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Edownloaded Ubuntu\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (there are plenty of different Linux distributions to choose from, but Ubuntu is one of the most popular distros for casual users) onto a USB drive. If you wanted to try Linux before fully committing to replacing your OS with it, it is possible to run any distribution from a thumb drive. Since I was going to be doing this experiment for a month and wanted to have access to the computers storage space, I opted to wipe the computer and install Linux. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOn my home PC, I have two terabytes of hard drive space, so I had more than enough room to host two operating systems side by side and still have a decent amount of storage allocated to each OS. When partitioning a disk to run both Windows\u002FMacOS and Linux on the same computer, you can choose how much of your hard drive you want to allocate to each OS. In my case I chose to split it evenly. Now, whenever I reboot that PC, it will automatically boot into Windows, but if I enter the boot menu after restarting the computer, I can also choose to boot into Linux instead.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIn spite of the easy of installation and compatibility with most software programs, Ubuntu and other Linux operating systems \u003Ci\u003E still\u003C\u002Fi\u003E havent really taken off in the mainstream. The reason for this, I think, is that using Linux actually feels like using a computeras in, the remarkably complex network of transistors, logic gates, and the other stuff ensconced whatever device youre reading this on. Linux violates the first rule of getting people to use a technology, which is that it shouldnt feel like youre using technology at all. To paraphrase Arthur C. Clarke, it should feel like magic. Linux does not feel like magic; it feels like a pain in the assat least until youve figured out how to use a command terminal.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EWeve gotten so accustomed to graphical user interfaces that most of us have forgotten that prior to the mid-80s, most computers didnt have application icons that could summon advanced programs with a double tap on a mouse. Instead, pulling a document from a file or launching a program required the user to actually enter the desired command as text. The latest version of Ubuntu has a sleek graphical interface that isnt that much different from what youd find on Windows or MacOS, but after a few days of learning command terminal its hard to go back.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIts \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.networkworld.com\u002Farticle\u002F3091139\u002Flinux\u002Fwho-needs-a-gui-how-to-live-in-a-linux-terminal.htm\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Epossible to do basically everything\u003C\u002Fa\u003E from a Linux terminal, but just because its possible doesnt necessarily mean you want to. Learning to effectively use the terminal was definitely the most gratifying part of my experiment. Although I am still a novice, I really liked that it allowed me to tell the computer exactly what I wanted it to do, without having to navigate endless menus or other superfluous features. It felt like I had real control over my computer, as opposed to being forced to use applications based on what the designers thought their users wanted. I also learned a great deal about how an operating system actually works by having to think through directory structures and follow logical sequences of commands.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EStill, the first few days of using Linux were incredibly frustrating. It felt like I had to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fen.wikipedia.org\u002Fwiki\u002FGoogle_(verb)\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EGoogle\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eahem, \u003Ci\u003E query \u003C\u002Fi\u003Eon DuckDuckGothe answer for the simplest things, such as how to download an application. At this point, Ubuntu has a pretty extensive package repository, so many programs you use on a regular basis are probably one-click downloads. But if you want to run a more obscure program, youre going to have to compile it yourself from the source, which includes learning how to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.howtogeek.com\u002F105413\u002Fhow-to-compile-and-install-from-source-on-ubuntu\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emake a directory and all that good stuff\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EOther than my initial difficulties with the terminal, the Linux experience with Ubuntu was quite pleasant. There are alternative open source programs for pretty much everything youd find on a Windows system. For example, LibreOffice is a perfect substitute for Word, Excel, and Powerpoint, GIMP is a more than adequate substitute for Adobe Photoshop for amateur photo editing, and Pidgin is a great instant messaging app. If you absolutely need to run Windows programs on a Linux machine, theres an app called Wine that will let you do just that. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThere are also a number of other hidden advantages that come with Linux. For starters, it is arguably the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.computerworld.com\u002Farticle\u002F3252823\u002Flinux\u002Fwhy-linux-is-better-than-windows-or-macos-for-security.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emost secure OS\u003C\u002Fa\u003Eyou probably \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.howtogeek.com\u002F135392\u002Fhtg-explains-why-you-dont-need-an-antivirus-on-linux-and-when-you-do\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Edont even need an anti-virus program\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Ubuntu, along with and other Linux distributions, is generally an ultra-efficient and lean operating system, so if you are using an older computer like I was, you shouldnt have any trouble running it. Best of all, its entirely free. This was a breath of fresh air after using Microsoft, which will charge you an arm and a leg for Windows (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.microsoft.com\u002Fen-us\u002Fp\u002Fwindows-10-home\u002Fd76qx4bznwk4\u002F1NT3\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E$139 for the home edition\u003C\u002Fa\u003E) and then still more for its defining features, such as Microsoft Office (\u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fproducts.office.com\u002Fen-us\u002Fbuy\u002Foffice\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E$70 for a single user home edition\u003C\u002Fa\u003E).\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Ch2 class=\"text-center\"\u003E HOW TO QUIT GOOGLE\u003C\u002Fh2\u003E \u003Cp\u003EGoogle was without a doubt the hardest company to purge from my life, but for this reason, also the most necessary. I am dependent on Google products for almost everything in my personal and professional life. At work, my editors and I workshop stories in Google docs; our company email system is hosted on Gmail servers; my contact with people at VICE that dont directly work with Motherboard is almost exclusively through Hangouts; I organize calls with sources on Google Calendar; all my documents and photos are automatically synced to Google Drive; I frequently write about videos I find on YouTube; Google Maps is only way I know how to navigate New York City; Googles Authenticator app secures many of my most important online accounts; Chrome has been my web browser since it was released a decade ago; and most importantly, my phone, and 75 percent of all the other phones on the planet, run Android, which is mainly developed by Google.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EIn some cases, Googles products are far better than anything else out there (Google Maps) or are seemingly irreplaceable because thats what everyone else uses (YouTube). Yet the real attraction to Google is that all of its products are seamlessly integrated across devices. The idea of unlinking all these vital aspects of my professional and personal life was off-putting, and trying to find adequate replacements for all these services seemed nearly impossible. But I am here to tell you that there is life after Google.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E GMAIL\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThe easiest Google product to ditch was Gmail because there are plenty of good alternative email providers out there. I opted to go with Protonmail, a Swiss email provider that encrypts every email sent through its service. The only downside I noticed was that I used up approximately half of my allotted 500 MB of free storage space in the month. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIt is, of course, possible to do a paid subscription and upgrade to get more storage, but this costs significantly more than Gmail's storage upgrades, which also allows for file hosting through Google Drive. For the sake of comparison, 5 GB of storage on Protonmail costs a little over $5\u002Fmonth, whereas Google charges $2\u002Fmonth for 100 GB. This is the economics of scale at work. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough it is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fjeffreifman.com\u002Fhow-to-install-your-own-private-e-mail-server-in-the-amazon-cloud-aws\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Epossible to set up your own email server\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, this process is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.geekwire.com\u002F2015\u002Fwhy-you-shouldnt-try-to-host-your-own-email\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Equite complex\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, though there are a few startups that are trying to streamline the process. If you havent set up a web server before (more on this below), try doing that first before making the leap to hosting your own email. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003ERather than going through the hassle of deleting all my Gmail accounts for a month, I set up my Gmail accounts to automatically forward incoming mail to my new Protonmail accounts, so technically Google was still processing my email. For anyone looking to permanently ditch Gmail youll still probably want to forward your emails to your new email account at first so that you dont end up missing anything important while your contacts catch up to your new email address. Another option is to send out a mass email informing your contacts of your new address.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E GOOGLE DRIVE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMy professional and personal life is such that I have amassed a substantial collection of documents, voice recordings, photographs, and other digital flotsam. To help keeps tabs on data distributed across several devices and to guard against data loss through hard drive destruction, I used a paid subscription to Google Drive. This got me a whopping 100 GB of storage space on Googles servers for a couple bucks a month, but the real cost was a substantial loss of privacy. Google automatically \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fzmz3yw\u002Fwhy-is-my-google-doc-locked-terms-of-service-bug\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Escans the contents of its user documents stored on Drive\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to prevent violations of its terms of service and serve up targeted ads. Up until last year it also \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.nytimes.com\u002F2017\u002F06\u002F23\u002Ftechnology\u002Fgmail-ads.html\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Escanned personal Gmail accounts\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough I always had the option of moving my personal documents to a different hosting device or to a local hard drive, this always seemed to be more hassle than it was worth since half of my job takes place in Google Docs, which my editors and I use for collaborative editing. Google Drive was convenient because it allows for collaboration on documents and storage in the same spot.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EThere are several great alternative cloud hosting services available, but far fewer alternative web services for collaborating on documents. One of the best known open source collaborative editors is Etherpad, which launched in 2008...and was \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnet.com\u002Fnews\u002Fgoogle-acquires-etherpad-online-collaboration-tool\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ealmost immediately acquired by Google\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI opted to try\u003Ca href=\"http:\u002F\u002Fpiratepad.net\u002Ffront-page\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E Piratepad\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, a fork of Etherpad that was created by the Swedish Pirate Party. Although I loved the spirit of Piratepad, its barebones format made editing articles difficult because it was harder to leave comments and make suggestions on articles. Instead, you had to make changes directly in the document. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMoreover, whenever I tried to copy an article from Piratepad into VICEs content management system, the format was totally wonky and reformatting the article added a substantial amount of time to the publishing process. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThe solution my editors and I eventually landed on was far from ideal. I would write an article locally using LibreOffice Writer (the Linux equivalent of Word), send the document in Slack to my editors, who would upload it to Google Drive on their own computers, edit it, re-download it as an ODT filethe file format for text documents in LibreOfficethen send it back to me on Slack for rewrites. Despite how wildly inefficient this was, it allowed for all the editing amenities found in Google Docs without messing with the articles format. Although this worked well enough for the month, its hard to imagine that this would be sustainable long term. As far as I could tell, when it comes to collaborative editing software theres still no good replacement for Google Docs. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EAs for the hosting platform, I decided to use NextCloud, an open source fork of the file hosting service ownCloud. I was pleasantly surprised at how intuitive NextClouds interface was and how easy it was to integrate across my devices, including my rooted phone. NextCloud is run out of Germany, but because it is open source software, anyone can host their own file storage server locally and not rely on it. This only requires about $40 in set-up costs for a Raspberry Pi, a storage medium such as an external hard drive, and an ethernet cord. This sounds complicated, but there are plenty of \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fownyourbits.com\u002Fnextcloudpi\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eeasy-to-follow tutorials\u003C\u002Fa\u003E to set up your own cloud storage system at home. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E MAPS\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThere was a point in my life where I knew how to use a compass and read a topological map, but whatever part of my brain was reserved for storing this information started to atrophy the day I discovered Google Maps. This app is, without question, the best map app in existence, which makes sense given \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fpogue.blogs.nytimes.com\u002F2012\u002F09\u002F27\u002Fwhat-makes-googles-maps-so-good\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ehow much Google has invested in mapping technology\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. The company has fleets of cars with cameras mounted on them that roam the worlds streets, but its most important data is anonymously submitted by millions of users whose smartphones deliver movement data to Google as they navigate a city. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAt this point I couldnt locate my own ass without consulting Google Maps, so the prospect of trying to navigate New York Citya city I had moved to only a few months priorwithout this cartographic crutch was daunting. Last year, a cartographer named Justin OBeirne published a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.justinobeirne.com\u002Fgoogle-maps-moat\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Efascinating deep dive\u003C\u002Fa\u003E into why Googles maps are so good and why every competitor, including Apple, has found Google Maps to be basically impossible to replicate, so I knew going in I was going to experience a serious downgrade in navigation capabilities.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDespite this, there are plenty of alternative map apps to choose from. The three best alternatives, Apple Maps and Waze were off-limits because they are owned by Apple and Google, respectively. (I was also under the impression that Here was still owned by Nokia (Microsoft), but have since learned that it was sold to a consortium of German automakers in 2015.) I remembered the days when MapQuest was still considered the go-to for navigation, so I opted to use its service, figuring it probably got better over the years. If it has, it was hard to tell. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOne of the most convenient things about Google Maps is that it integrates various forms of transportation into its directions. Youll get different directions depending on whether youre biking, taking a car, walking, or taking the subway. MapQuest, however, only offers driving and walking, which is less than ideal in a city where public transit and biking are major modes of transportation. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThroughout the month, I found myself getting frustrated with little things like having to figure out the crossroads of a subway stop, rather than just typing in the name of the stop to get MapQuest to understand where I was. Likewise, I ended up taking a lot of inefficient bike routes because the MapQuest app couldnt tell me which streets had bike lanes. Theres something really nice about only having to type in library in Google Maps to get directed to New York Public Library a few blocks away. Unless you type out the full New York Public Library in MapQuest, youre liable to get directions to a library in another state. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E CHROME\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAbandoning Chrome was more of an annoyance than anything. Ive surfed the web using Googles browser for a while now after years of being a devoted Firefox user. Although I still had Firefox installed on my laptop, it wasnt nearly as perfectly tuned as my Chrome settings were. I mostly kept it around to use when I had to visit a site that insisted I turn off my various ad blockers and anti-tracking plugins I use on Chrome. The main reason I left Firefox a few years ago \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.extremetech.com\u002Fcomputing\u002F178587-firefox-is-still-the-least-secure-web-browser-falls-to-four-zero-day-exploits-at-pwn2own\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ewas its lackluster security\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.theregister.co.uk\u002F2018\u002F01\u002F24\u002Fmozilla_firefox_security_updates\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eslowly improving\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAlthough I also briefly used Opera and Brave for this experiment, I ultimately settled on Firefox as my go-to browser. Opera and Brave are both based on Chromium, the underlying engine for Googles Chrome browser. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDespite being open source, Firefox is not entirely Google-free, either. For the past decade, Mozilla has had an \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Ftechcrunch.com\u002F2008\u002F08\u002F28\u002Fmozilla-extends-lucrative-deal-with-google-for-3-years\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eoff-and-on agreement\u003C\u002Fa\u003E with Google to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.bloomberg.com\u002Fnews\u002Farticles\u002F2017-11-14\u002Fgoogle-pays-to-put-search-engine-back-on-firefox-browser-in-u-s\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Euse its search engine by default\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, which is quite lucrative for Mozilla. Still, it \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fblog.mozilla.org\u002Fblog\u002F2018\u002F12\u002F06\u002Fgoodbye-edge\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ewasnt running Googles engine\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, so I opted to use it for the majority of my experiment. As far as user experience was concerned, switching to Firefox was hardly a noticeable change. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E GOOGLE SEARCH\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EThere are plenty of alternative search engines out there, but the two leading candidatesBing and Google Searchwere off limits. For my experiment, I opted for DuckDuckGo, a privacy-oriented search engine. DuckDuckGo doesnt track your searches nor serve you targeted ads. Its hardly any wonder, then, that it is the default search engine for the TOR network. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003EDuckDuckGo also replicates a lot of features found in Google search, such as autocomplete and a command that allows you to directly search a website through the browser. For instance, if I were to type !imdb the most unknown, Id find myself on IMDBs page for Motherboards first documentary, \u003Ci\u003E The Most Unknown. \u003C\u002Fi\u003EOf course I wouldnt have done that, however, because IMDB is owned by Amazon.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EWhile I appreciated these features, I couldnt help but notice a remarkable deterioration in the quality of my search results compared to Google. With Google, I can type in a loose collection of keywords and usually find my desired result. With DuckDuckGo, my searches would have to be painstakingly exact. This made things difficult when I didnt know exactly what I was looking for, and constantly made me wonder if there were better search results that I wasnt seeing. In any case, DuckDuckGo was still pretty impressive and it felt good to know I wasnt being tracked every time I put something in the search bar. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EDespite its best intentions and willingness to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.theverge.com\u002F2018\u002F7\u002F20\u002F17595612\u002Fgoogle-antitrust-eu-duckduckgo-chrome\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ecall Google to task for its monopolizing business practices\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, DuckDuckGo is not entirely free from the grips of the Big Five. According to the company, DuckDuckGo makes money by \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fduck.co\u002Fhelp\u002Fcompany\u002Fadvertising-and-affiliates\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Eserving ads from the Yahoo-Microsoft search alliance\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. While these ads are based on the search query, rather than data about the user, at least a portion of DuckDuckGos revenue comes from Microsofts pockets. DuckDuckGo also is part of the Amazon affiliate program, so if you purchase Amazon products using the search engine the company earns a small commission. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E YOUTUBE\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EA significant part of my job involves watching YouTube videos, so I had to figure out a way to still get access to them without routing my traffic through the website. In May, there was a really convenient service around called Hooktube that could do just that. To use HookTube, you simply replaced the youtube portion in any YouTube video link with hooktube. Thats it. When you used HookTube, you wouldnt be routing traffic through Googles servers, giving views to the videos, or seeing any ads. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EOf course, all these videos still exist on Googles servers and HookTube would be useless without them. This is yet another case where there is really no real replacement for YouTube in terms of the sheer amount of content hosted on the site. There are plenty of other video platforms (Vimeo, for example) but they have differentand vastly smallervideo libraries.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EI really fell in love with HookTube, but unfortunately the service is no more. As detailed in \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fhooktube.com\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EHookTubes changelog\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, on July 16 the service was ended due to increasing pressure from YouTubes legal team. Although HookTube still exists, its links are routed through Googles servers. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EHookTube is now effectively just a lightweight version of YouTube and useless to the 90 percent of you primarily concerned with denying Google data and seeing videos blocked by your governments, the changelog reads. Rest in pieces. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIn the meantime, others have attempted to make \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.reddit.com\u002Fr\u002Fprivacy\u002Fcomments\u002F903pxf\u002Fhooktube_is_no_more_so_i_made_a_similar_site\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ereplacement versions of HookTube\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. Some of these appear to work well, but as HookTube demonstrated, its only a matter of time before they attract the attention of YouTubes legal department. While its certainly possible to create an endless array of mirror sites to avoid censorship from internet service providers, similar to how torrenting sites such as Pirate Bay continue to operate despite a crackdown on torrenting, no one appears to have done the same with HookTube yet. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E AUTHENTICATOR\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIf youre thinking of ditching Google and you use two-factor authentication to secure your accounts, \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fevknva\u002Fwhat-is-a-two-factor-authentication-recovery-code\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Emake sure you have your recovery code for every account secured using Google Authenticator\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. If you do not have these, \u003Cb\u003E you will be locked out of your account. \u003C\u002Fb\u003EI cannot emphasize how important it is to triple check that you have a backup way to get into accounts secured with two-factor authentication when leaving Google. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EWhile I wouldnt suggest reverting to SMS-based verification, which \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fvbqax3\u002Fhackers-sim-swapping-steal-phone-numbers-instagram-bitcoin\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Ecan be spoofed by attackers\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, there is a good alternative two-factor authentication service out there called Authy.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp class=\"article__blockquote\"\u003E\u003Cb\u003E Read More: \u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fmotherboard.vice.com\u002Fen_us\u002Farticle\u002Fevknva\u002Fwhat-is-a-two-factor-authentication-recovery-code\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E \u003Cb\u003E What Is a Two-Factor Authentication Recovery Code?\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fa\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAuthy can be used on any site that supports Authenticator, but it comes with a few distinct advantages, the most notable being that it has multiple-device functionality. Authenticator is tied to a single device, so if you want to use it on your phone and tablet at the same time, youre out of luck. Youll have to \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.cnet.com\u002Fhow-to\u002Fhow-to-move-google-authenticator-to-a-new-device\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Etransfer all of your accounts to the new device\u003C\u002Fa\u003E. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAuthy allows you to have the service on multiple devices, so if you lose your phone and havent backed up your seeds like I told you to, youll still be able to get back into your devices. (Importantly, you can also disable Authy on the lost device.) Moreover, Authenticator only works on mobile devices, whereas Authy works on desktops and laptops as well.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003E\u003Cb\u003E ANDROID\u003C\u002Fb\u003E \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EWhen I arrived home from the Verizon store with my Samsung Galaxy S3, I immediately set to work trying to figure out how to get Sailfish OS on it. Sailfish is perhaps the last truly independent mobile operating system availableFirefox OS, Windows Phone, and Ubuntu Mobile have all bitten the dust in the past few years. At this point, only about 0.1 percent of all smartphones arent running iOS or Android. If I were going to truly ditch Google, I was going to have to ditch Android as well.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAndroid is nominally open source, but it is \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.slashdata.co\u002Fblog\u002F2011\u002F07\u002Fthe-open-governance-index-measuring-openness-from-android-to-webkit\" target=\"_blank\"\u003Efar from free open source software\u003C\u002Fa\u003E in any meaningful sense. Google has maintained the \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fsource.android.com\u002F\" target=\"_blank\"\u003EAndroid Open Source Project\u003C\u002Fa\u003E (AOSP) since it acquired Android in 2005. Googles software engineers are responsible for new releases of the Android operating system. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EAndroid is based on the Linux kernel, the part of an operating system responsible for interfacing with the devices hardware and managing the computers resources such as CPU and RAM. This source code is released for free through AOSP, so anyone can take the Android code made by Google developers and use it to make their own version of Android. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EWhen you buy a phone, the Android OS that comes with it also has a bunch of services grafted on top. These are the Google Mobile Services (GMS) that many users take to be defining features Android: Google search, Maps, Drive, Gmail, and so on. These services are definitely not open source.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cdiv class=\"ad-unit__container__container\"\u003E\u003Cdiv class=\"article-iac__wrapper\"\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003C\u002Fdiv\u003E\u003Cp\u003ESo why does this matter if anyone can modify Android code, or fork it, any time they want? Even if someone managed to fork Android and clone all its best apps, theyd be hard-pressed to find a manufacturer to build a device for this Android clone. As Ben Edelman, an associate professor at Harvard Business School, explained in a \u003Ca href=\"https:\u002F\u002Fwww.hbs.edu\u002Ffaculty\u002FPublication%20Files\u002F17-018_b0371672-7aa4-452a-8497-1cccebd9657a.pdf\" target=\"_blank\"\u003E2016 paper\u003C\u002Fa\u003E, device manufacturers are free to produce phones running bare versions of Android, but this means no Google apps are allowed to be pre-installed on the device. \u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EIf the device manufacturer wants to include Google Mobile Services on its Android phones, it must sign a Mobile Application Distribution Agreement that requires it to pre-install certain Google applications in prominent places, such as the phones home page. Google search must also be set as the default search provider for all web access points. Google also requires that its Network Location Provider service be preloaded and the default, tracking users geographic location at all times and sending that information to Google.\u003C\u002Fp\u003E \u003Cp\u003EMore troubling is that Google makes all device manufacturers that want to run Google Mobile Services on their devices sign an Anti-Fragmentation Agreement (AFA). This is a legal agreement that states the manufacturers wont fork their own version of Android to run on their devices. As Edelman notes, no copies of this agreement have ever been leaked to the public, even though the existence of the document has been confirmed by Google.
